     <p>The <b>University of California, Santa Barbara</b> (commonly referred to as <b>UC Santa Barbara</b> or <b>UCSB</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> research university and one of the 10 general campuses of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> system. The main campus is located on a 1,022-acre (414&nbsp;ha) site in <a href="/wiki/Goleta,_California" title="Goleta, California">Goleta, California</a>, United States, 8 miles (13&nbsp;km) from <a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara,_California" title="Santa Barbara, California">Santa Barbara</a> and 100 miles (160&nbsp;km) northwest of Los Angeles. Tracing its roots back to 1891 as an independent teachers' college, UCSB joined the University of California system in 1944 and is the third-oldest general-education campus in the system.</p> 
     <p>UCSB is one of America's <a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a> universities, which recognizes top public research universities in the United States. The university is a comprehensive doctoral university and is organized into five colleges and schools offering 87 undergraduate degrees and 55 graduate degrees. The campus is the 6th-largest in the UC system by enrollment with 18,977 undergraduate and 2,950 graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-CommonDataSet-B_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CommonDataSet-B-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, UCSB was ranked 41st among &quot;National Universities&quot; and 10th among public universities by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-US_News_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_News-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was also ranked 35th worldwide by the <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> and 34th worldwide (6th worldwide for engineering) by the <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-ShanghaiRanking.com_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShanghaiRanking.com-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shanghairanking.com.2FFieldENG2012_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shanghairanking.com.2FFieldENG2012-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC Santa Barbara is a &quot;very high activity&quot; research university and spent $191.2 million on research expenditures in the 2007 fiscal year, 97th-largest in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-NSF_R.26D_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSF_R.26D-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSB houses twelve national research centers,<sup id="cite_ref-ucsb.edu_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucsb.edu-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> including the renowned <a href="/wiki/Kavli_Institute_for_Theoretical_Physics" title="Kavli Institute for Theoretical Physics">Kavli Institute for Theoretical Physics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSB faculty includes five <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> laureates, one <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medalist</a>, 29 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a>, 27 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>, and 31 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSB was the No. 3 host on the <a href="/wiki/ARPAnet" title="ARPAnet" class="mw-redirect">ARPAnet</a> and was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> in 1995.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/UC_Santa_Barbara_Gauchos" title="UC Santa Barbara Gauchos">UC Santa Barbara Gauchos</a> compete in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> <a href="/wiki/Big_West_Conference" title="Big West Conference">Big West Conference</a>. The Gauchos have won NCAA national championships in men's soccer and men's water polo.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara" title="History of the University of California, Santa Barbara">History of the University of California, Santa Barbara</a>
     </div> 
     <p>UCSB traces its origins back to the Anna Blake School which was founded in 1891 and offered training in home economics and industrial arts.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A_note_on_histories_of_SBCC.2C_UCSB_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_note_on_histories_of_SBCC.2C_UCSB-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The Anna Blake School was taken over by the state in 1909 and became the Santa Barbara State Normal School. Intense lobbying by an interest group in the City of Santa Barbara, led by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Storke" title="Thomas Storke" class="mw-redirect">Thomas Storke</a> and Pearl Chase, persuaded the State Legislature, Governor <a href="/wiki/Earl_Warren" title="Earl Warren">Earl Warren</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">Regents of the University of California</a> to move the State College over to the more research-oriented University of California system in 1944. The State College system sued to stop the takeover, but the Governor did not support the suit. A state initiative was passed, however, to stop subsequent conversions of State Colleges to University of California campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-stadtman_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stadtman-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> From 1944 to 1958 the school was known as Santa Barbara College of the University of California, before taking on its current name. When the vacated Marine Corps training station in Goleta was purchased for the rapidly-growing college, Santa Barbara City College moved into the vacated State College buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-Baker.2C_Gayle.2C_p._83_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker.2C_Gayle.2C_p._83-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Originally, the Regents envisioned a small, several thousand-student liberal arts college, a so-called &quot;<a href="/wiki/Williams_College" title="Williams College">Williams College</a> of the West&quot;, at Santa Barbara. Chronologically, UCSB is the third general-education campus of the University of California, after Berkeley and UCLA (the only other state campus to have been acquired by the UC system). The original campus the Regents acquired in Santa Barbara was located on only 100 acres (40&nbsp;ha) of largely unusable land on a seaside mesa. The availability of a 400-acre (160&nbsp;ha) portion of the land used as <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Air_Station_Santa_Barbara" title="Marine Corps Air Station Santa Barbara">Marine Corps Air Station Santa Barbara</a> until 1946 on another seaside mesa in <a href="/wiki/Goleta,_California" title="Goleta, California">Goleta</a>, which the Regents could acquire for free from the federal government, led to that site becoming the Santa Barbara campus in 1949. Originally, only 3000?3500 students were anticipated, but the post WWII <a href="/wiki/Baby_boom" title="Baby boom">baby boom</a> led to the designation of general campus in 1958, along with a name change from &quot;Santa Barbara College&quot; to &quot;University of California, Santa Barbara,&quot; and the discontinuation of the industrial arts program for which the State college was famous. A <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_(education)" title="Chancellor (education)">Chancellor</a>, Samuel B. Gould, was appointed in 1959. All of this change was done in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/California_Master_Plan_for_Higher_Education" title="California Master Plan for Higher Education">California Master Plan for Higher Education</a>.</p> 
     <p>In 1959, UCSB Professor Douwe Stuurman hosted the English writer <a href="/wiki/Aldous_Huxley" title="Aldous Huxley">Aldous Huxley</a> as the university's first visiting professor.<sup id="cite_ref-The_50th_Anniversary_of_Aldous_Huxley.E2.80.99s_UCSB_Lecture_Series_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_50th_Anniversary_of_Aldous_Huxley.E2.80.99s_UCSB_Lecture_Series-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Huxley delivered a lectures series called &quot;The Human Situation&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the late 1960s and early 1970s UCSB became nationally known as a hotbed of anti-Vietnam War activity. A bombing at the school's faculty club in 1969 killed the caretaker, Dover Sharp. In the spring 1970 multiple occasions of arson occurred, including a burning of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a> branch building in the student community of <a href="/wiki/Isla_Vista" title="Isla Vista" class="mw-redirect">Isla Vista</a>, during which time one male student, Kevin Moran, was shot and killed by police.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSB's anti-Vietnam activity impelled then Governor <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a> to impose a <a href="/wiki/Curfew" title="Curfew">curfew</a> and order the <a href="/wiki/California_National_Guard" title="California National Guard">National Guard</a> to enforce it. Weapon-carrying guardsmen were a common sight on campus and in Isla Vista during this time.</p> 
     <p>In 1995, UCSB was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, an organization of leading research universities, with a membership consisting of 59 universities in the United States (both <a href="/wiki/State_university_system_(United_States)" title="State university system (United States)" class="mw-redirect">public</a> and <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a>) and two universities in Canada.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Provosts_and_Chancellors">Provosts and Chancellors</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Provosts and Chancellors">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li>1944?1946 <a href="/wiki/Clarence_L._Phelps" title="Clarence L. Phelps">Clarence L. Phelps</a></li> 
      <li>1946?1955 <a href="/wiki/J._Harold_Williams" title="J. Harold Williams">J. Harold Williams</a></li> 
      <li>1955?1955 <a href="/wiki/Clark_G._Kuebler" title="Clark G. Kuebler">Clark G. Kuebler</a></li> 
      <li>1956?1956 <a href="/wiki/John_C._Snidecor" title="John C. Snidecor">John C. Snidecor</a></li> 
      <li>1956?1959 <a href="/wiki/Elmer_Noble" title="Elmer Noble">Elmer Noble</a></li> 
      <li>1959?1962 <a href="/wiki/Samuel_B._Gould" title="Samuel B. Gould">Samuel B. Gould</a></li> 
      <li>1962?1977 <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Cheadle" title="Vernon Cheadle">Vernon Cheadle</a></li> 
      <li>1977?1986 <a href="/wiki/Robert_Huttenback" title="Robert Huttenback">Robert Huttenback</a></li> 
      <li>1986?1987 <a href="/wiki/Daniel_G._Aldrich" title="Daniel G. Aldrich">Daniel G. Aldrich</a></li> 
      <li>1987?1994 <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Uehling" title="Barbara Uehling">Barbara Uehling</a></li> 
      <li>1994?present <a href="/wiki/Henry_T._Yang" title="Henry T. Yang">Henry T. Yang</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/California_State_University#Former_campuses" title="California State University">Santa Barbara State College</a> was under the supervision of a President, but in 1944, when it became a campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a>, the title of the chief executive was changed to <a href="/wiki/Provost_(education)" title="Provost (education)">Provost</a>. In September 1958, the <a href="/wiki/Regents_of_the_University_of_California" title="Regents of the University of California">Regents of the University of California</a> established Santa Barbara as a general University campus and at the official title of the chief executive was changed to <a href="/wiki/Chancellor" title="Chancellor">Chancellor</a>. UCSB's first Provost was thus <a href="/wiki/Clarence_L._Phelps" title="Clarence L. Phelps">Clarence L. Phelps</a>, while UCSB's first Chancellor was <a href="/wiki/Samuel_B._Gould" title="Samuel B. Gould">Samuel B. Gould</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara_campus" title="University of California, Santa Barbara campus">University of California, Santa Barbara campus</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Ucsbuniversitycenterandstorketower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Ucsbuniversitycenterandstorketower.jpg/300px-Ucsbuniversitycenterandstorketower.jpg" width="300" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Ucsbuniversitycenterandstorketower.jpg/450px-Ucsbuniversitycenterandstorketower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Ucsbuniversitycenterandstorketower.jpg/600px-Ucsbuniversitycenterandstorketower.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Ucsbuniversitycenterandstorketower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Storke_Tower" title="Storke Tower">Storke Tower</a> and the University Center in front of the UCSB Lagoon.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UCSB_06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/UCSB_06.JPG/300px-UCSB_06.JPG" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/UCSB_06.JPG/450px-UCSB_06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/UCSB_06.JPG/600px-UCSB_06.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UCSB_06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A view over the school's lagoon to one of the Channel Islands
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>UCSB is located on cliffs directly above the Pacific Ocean. UCSB's campus is completely autonomous from local government and has not been annexed by the city of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara,_California" title="Santa Barbara, California">Santa Barbara</a> and thus is not part of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-annex_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annex-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ellwood_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ellwood-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> While it appears closer to the recently formed city of <a href="/wiki/Goleta,_California" title="Goleta, California">Goleta</a>, a parcel of the City of Santa Barbara that forms a strip of &quot;city&quot; through the ocean to the Santa Barbara airport, runs through the west entrance to the university campus. Although UCSB has a Santa Barbara mailing address, as do other unincorporated areas around the city, only this entry parcel is in the Santa Barbara city limits. Like all other UC and CSU campuses, it is self-governing and cannot be incorporated into either city. The campus is divided into four parts: Main (East) Campus 708 acres (287&nbsp;ha) that houses all academic units plus the majority of undergraduate housing, Storke Campus, West Campus and North Campus. The campuses surround the community of <a href="/wiki/Isla_Vista,_California" title="Isla Vista, California">Isla Vista</a>.</p> 
     <p>UCSB is one of a few universities in the United States with its own beach. The campus, bordered on three sides by the Pacific Ocean, has miles of coastline as well as its own lagoon. The campus has numerous walking and bicycle paths across campus, around the lagoon and along the beach.</p> 
     <p>Much of the campus' early architecture was designed by famed architect <a href="/wiki/William_Pereira" title="William Pereira">William Pereira</a> and his partner <a href="/wiki/Charles_Luckman" title="Charles Luckman">Charles Luckman</a>, and made heavy use of custom tinted and patterned concrete block. This design element was carried over into many of the school's subsequent buildings.</p> 
     <p>The Lagoon is a large body of water adjacent to the coastline, between San Rafael and San Miguel Residence Halls. It was created from a former tidal salt marsh flat and is fed by a combination of run-off and ocean water used by the Marine Science Building's aquatic life tanks; thus, it is a unique combination of fresh and salt water. Many of the older campus buildings are being replaced with newer, more modern facilities. The <a href="/wiki/UCSB_Libraries" title="UCSB Libraries" class="mw-redirect">UCSB Libraries</a>, consisting of the Davidson Library and the Arts Library, hold more than 3 million bound volumes<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> and millions of <a href="/wiki/Microform" title="Microform">microforms</a>, government documents, manuscripts, maps, satellite and aerial images, sound recordings, and other materials. Situated at the center of campus, the UCSB Library will break ground on a significant addition and renovation project in June 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Campbell Hall is the university's largest lecture hall with 862 seats. It is also the main venue for the UCSB Arts and Lectures series, which presents special performances, films, and lectures for the UCSB campus and Santa Barbara community.</p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Storke_Tower" title="Storke Tower">Storke Tower</a>, completed in 1969, is the tallest building in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara_County" title="Santa Barbara County" class="mw-redirect">Santa Barbara County</a>. It can be seen from most places on campus, and it overlooks Storke Plaza. It is home to a five-octave, 61-bell <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">carillon</a>. <a href="/wiki/KCSB_91.9FM_Santa_Barbara" title="KCSB 91.9FM Santa Barbara" class="mw-redirect">KCSB 91.9</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Nexus" title="Daily Nexus">Daily Nexus</a></i> have headquarters beneath Storke Tower.</p> 
     <p>The UCSB Family Vacation Center founded in 1969, is a summer family camp located on campus that draws over 2,000 guests each summer. The staff of over 50 includes many UCSB students who have been extensively trained as camp counselors.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Layout">Layout</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Layout">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university (itself termed a &quot;campus&quot; of the University of California) is divided into two physical campuses, a West Campus and East Campus. The vast majority of university facilities, including all lecture halls and laboratories, are in the East Campus. The two campuses are connected by a large strip (known as the North and Storke Campuses) to the north which contain university housing and athletic fields. Thus, the university surrounds Isla Vista on three sides.</p> 
     <p>West Campus, aside from a few buildings dedicated to faculty housing, has largely been leased out to private organizations, and includes a school for the mentally disabled and a large nature preserve. The largest sand dunes on the south-facing coast of the Santa Barbara Channel are located here.</p> 
     <p>The East Campus centers around two <a href="/wiki/Quadrangle_(architecture)" title="Quadrangle (architecture)">quadrangles</a>, separated from each other by the main library and bus circle, and the life sciences buildings. Along the western quad are Storke Plaza and buildings housing the various arts, social sciences, and humanities departments. The Student Resource Building and the Events Center are also located along this quad. Surrounding the wider, park-like eastern quad are buildings housing the physical sciences departments and the College of Engineering. Directly to the south of, but not adjacent to, the eastern quad are the life sciences and psychology departments, as well as most of the on-campus housing. The southernmost section of the campus is dominated by the lagoon. The peninsula extending from the beach into the lagoon contains an elaborate labyrinth.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycles">Bicycles</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Bicycles">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UCSB is known for its extensive biking system. Bicycles <a href="/wiki/Segregated_cycle_facilities#Bikeways_that_use_independent_rights-of-way" title="Segregated cycle facilities">have exclusive right of way</a> on paths throughout East Campus. <a href="/wiki/Bicycle_stand" title="Bicycle stand" class="mw-redirect">Bicycle stands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bicycle_locker" title="Bicycle locker">lockers</a> are ubiquitous.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSB is unique among bicycle-heavy areas in that most travel is done within a small radius.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>UC Santa Barbara is a large, comprehensive, primarily residential doctoral university.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The full-time, four-year undergraduate program comprises the majority of enrollments and has an arts &amp; sciences focus with high graduate co-existence.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSB is organized into five colleges and schools offering 87 undergraduate degrees and 55 graduate degrees. The campus is the 6th-largest in the UC system by enrollment with 18,620 undergraduate and 3,065 graduate students.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>Admission to UC Santa Barbara is rated as &quot;most selective&quot; by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UC Santa Barbara received 54,832 applications for admission to the Fall 2012 incoming freshman class; 24,133 were admitted (44.0%).<sup id="cite_ref-bap.ucsb.edu_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bap.ucsb.edu-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Enrolled freshmen had an average high school <a href="/wiki/GPA" title="GPA" class="mw-redirect">GPA</a> of 3.91, and an average combined <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> score of 1852 (average SAT scores of 601 for Critical Reading, 633 for Mathematics, and 617 for Writing).<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> 25% of admitted students receive federal <a href="/wiki/Pell_grant" title="Pell grant" class="mw-redirect">Pell grants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_activity">Research activity</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Research activity">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>From 2005?2009, UCSB was ranked fourth in terms of relative citation impact in the U.S. (behind <a href="/wiki/MIT" title="MIT" class="mw-redirect">MIT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caltech" title="Caltech" class="mw-redirect">Caltech</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a>) according to <a href="/wiki/Thomson_Reuters" title="Thomson Reuters">Thomson Reuters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UCSB hosts 12 National Research Centers, including the <a href="/wiki/Kavli_Institute_for_Theoretical_Physics" title="Kavli Institute for Theoretical Physics">Kavli Institute for Theoretical Physics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Ecological_Analysis_and_Synthesis" title="National Center for Ecological Analysis and Synthesis">National Center for Ecological Analysis and Synthesis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_California_Earthquake_Center" title="Southern California Earthquake Center">Southern California Earthquake Center</a>, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://spatial.ucsb.edu/">Center for Spatial Studies</a>, an affiliate of the <a href="/wiki/National_Center_for_Geographic_Information_and_Analysis" title="National Center for Geographic Information and Analysis">National Center for Geographic Information and Analysis</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/California_Nanosystems_Institute" title="California Nanosystems Institute" class="mw-redirect">California Nanosystems Institute</a>. Eight of these centers are supported by the National Science Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-ucsb.edu_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucsb.edu-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSB is also home to <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Station_Q" title="Microsoft Station Q" class="mw-redirect">Microsoft Station Q</a>, a research group working on <a href="/wiki/Topological_quantum_computer" title="Topological quantum computer">topological quantum computing</a> where American mathematician and <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Freedman" title="Michael Freedman">Michael Freedman</a> is the director.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teaching_and_degrees">Teaching and degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Teaching and degrees">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The focus of the University of California is on research.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Like all University of California campuses, UCSB prioritizes academic development over vocational learning. Undergraduate teaching is centered on lectures, with larger lecture classes having sections. Sections may be tutorial style, or they may be set up as seminars or discussions. For undergraduates, UCSB confers both B.A. and B.S. degrees. Music majors may pursue a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Music" title="Bachelor of Music">Bachelor of Music</a> degree. Graduate teaching involves seminar style classes and an emphasis on research and further study. UCSB confers <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts_(postgraduate)" title="Master of Arts (postgraduate)" class="mw-redirect">M.A.</a>, M.S., and PhD degrees. Those studying music may pursue a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Music" title="Master of Music">M.M.</a> or <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Musical_Arts" title="Doctor of Musical Arts">D.M.A.</a> degree. Students pursuing a career in education may receive a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Education" title="Master of Education">M.Ed.</a> or <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Education" title="Doctor of Education">Ed.D.</a> degree. The university granted 5,812 bachelors, 578 masters, and 354 PhD degrees in 2010?2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Portrait_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portrait-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>UCSB is considered to be a &quot;<a href="/wiki/Public_Ivy" title="Public Ivy">Public Ivy</a>&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2013 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> ranked UC Santa Barbara as the 41st best university (and 10th best public university) in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-US_News_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_News-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013 <i><a href="/wiki/Kiplinger" title="Kiplinger">Kiplinger</a></i> ranked UCSB 14th out of the top 100 best-value public colleges and universities in the nation, and 4th in California.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_impact_rankings">Research impact rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Research impact rankings">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i> ranked UCSB 35th worldwide in 2012, 23rd in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> while the <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> (ARWU) ranked UCSB 34rd, 26th in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-ShanghaiRanking.com_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShanghaiRanking.com-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> ARWU ranked UCSB 6th worldwide for engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council_rankings" title="United States National Research Council rankings">United States National Research Council rankings</a> of graduate programs, 10 UCSB departments were ranked in the top ten in the country: Materials, Chemical Engineering, Computer Science, Electrical and Computer Engineering, Mechanical Engineering, <a href="/wiki/UC_Santa_Barbara_Physics_Department" title="UC Santa Barbara Physics Department">Physics</a>, Marine Science Institute, Geography, History, and Theater and Dance.<sup id="cite_ref-PhDs.org_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhDs.org-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Among US university Materials Science and Engineering programs, UCSB was ranked first in each mesure of a study by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council" title="United States National Research Council">National Research Council</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">NAS</a> <sup id="cite_ref-National_Research_Council_Materials_Ranking_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_Research_Council_Materials_Ranking-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <i>Centre for Science and Technologies Studies</i> at <a href="/wiki/Leiden_University" title="Leiden University">Leiden University</a> in the Netherlands ranked UCSB as the 7th best research university in the world based on Mean normalized citation score (MNCS), and as the 2nd best in the world based on the proportion of the publications to the top 10% most frequently cited.<sup id="cite_ref-Leiden_Ranking_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leiden_Ranking-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>The Global Research Report: United States</i> published by Thomson Reuters in November 2010 rated UCSB's research 4th nationally in citation impact.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Among US university economics programs, in 2010 UCSB was ranked the 6th for experimental economics, 3rd for environmental economics, and 12th for cognitive and behavioral economics by RePEc.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Monthly" title="Washington Monthly">Washington Monthly</a></i>, whose ranking focuses on public service and research impact, named UCSB as the 14th best national university in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_rankings">Other rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Other rankings">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Research_Council_rankings" title="United States National Research Council rankings">United States National Research Council rankings</a> of graduate programs, 10 UCSB departments were ranked in the top ten in the country: Materials, Chemical Engineering, Computer Science, Electrical and Computer Engineering, Mechanical Engineering, <a href="/wiki/UC_Santa_Barbara_Physics_Department" title="UC Santa Barbara Physics Department">Physics</a>, Marine Science Institute, Geography, History, and Theater and Dance.<sup id="cite_ref-PhDs.org_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PhDs.org-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>US News &amp; World Report</i> ranked UCSB's graduate programs in Materials Engineering and Chemical Engineering the 2nd and 8th best in the U.S., respectively; the graduate school for Physics was ranked 10th best, including the 3rd best program for Condensed Matter Physics, 5th best program for Quantum Physics and the 8th best program for Elementary Particles/Field/String Theory.<sup id="cite_ref-US_News_Rankings_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_News_Rankings-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> In terms of the social sciences, UCSB's graduate program in Sociology is ranked 2nd for research in sex and gender and 7th for sociology of culture; the History department is ranked 10th for women's history.<sup id="cite_ref-US_News_Rankings_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_News_Rankings-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UCSB's Department of Communication was recognized as top in the nation based on data from the National Research Council?s study.<sup id="cite_ref-Department_Ratings_.26_Rankings_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Department_Ratings_.26_Rankings-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Several areas in UCSB's Department of Communication have been Ranked Best in Nation by the National Communication Association. Specifically, UCSB's Department of Communication has been ranked number 1 in the nation for Interpersonal and Small Group Communication, number 1 in the nation for Intercultural/International Communication, number 2 in the nation Organizational Communication, number 4 in the nation for Communication and Technology, and number 17 in the nation for Mass Communication.<sup id="cite_ref-Department_Ratings_.26_Rankings_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Department_Ratings_.26_Rankings-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSB's Department of Communication has been ranked No. 3 in the nation in terms of research productivity, according to a recent analysis of scholarly articles that have appeared in eight academic journals sponsored by the National Communication Association and the International Communication Association.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, UCSB's Department of Communication has been named One of the Top High Impact Departments in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics</a> ranked UCSB 49th worldwide in its July 2012 ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-topuniversities_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-topuniversities-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> ranked UCSB 118th in the world.</p> 
     <p>The lowest ranking received by the university from a major publication comes from <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> which ranks the university 139th in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> That ranking focuses mainly on net positive financial impact, in contrast to other rankings, and generally ranks liberal arts colleges above most research universities.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Santa Barbara is one of the ten major campuses affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a>. The University of California is governed by a 26-member <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Regents" title="Board of Regents" class="mw-redirect">Board of Regents</a>, 18 of which are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_California" title="Governor of California">Governor of California</a> to 12-year terms, 7 serving as <i><a href="/wiki/Ex_officio" title="Ex officio" class="mw-redirect">ex officio</a></i> members, and a single student regent.<sup id="cite_ref-Governance_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Governance-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The position of Chancellor was created in 1952 to lead individual campuses. The Board of Regents appointed <a href="/wiki/Henry_T._Yang" title="Henry T. Yang">Henry T. Yang</a> to be the 5th Chancellor of the university in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_schools">Colleges and schools</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Colleges and schools">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/College_of_Creative_Studies" title="College of Creative Studies">College of Creative Studies</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UCSB_College_of_Engineering" title="UCSB College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/UCSB_College_of_Letters_%26_Science" title="UCSB College of Letters &amp; Science">College of Letters &amp; Science</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Bren_School_of_Environmental_Science_%26_Management" title="Bren School of Environmental Science &amp; Management">Bren School of Environmental Science &amp; Management</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Gevirtz_Graduate_School_of_Education" title="Gevirtz Graduate School of Education">Gevirtz Graduate School of Education</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>UC Santa Barbara has three colleges: the <a href="/wiki/UCSB_College_of_Letters_%26_Science" title="UCSB College of Letters &amp; Science">College of Letters &amp; Science</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UCSB_College_of_Engineering" title="UCSB College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Creative_Studies" title="College of Creative Studies">College of Creative Studies</a>. The College of Creative Studies offers students an alternative approach to education by supporting advanced, independent work in the arts, mathematics, and sciences. The campus also has two professional schools, the <a href="/wiki/Bren_School_of_Environmental_Science_%26_Management" title="Bren School of Environmental Science &amp; Management">Bren School of Environmental Science &amp; Management</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Bren_Hall" title="Bren Hall">Bren Hall</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Gevirtz_Graduate_School_of_Education" title="Gevirtz Graduate School of Education">Gevirtz Graduate School of Education</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_year">Academic year</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Academic year">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university runs on a <a href="/wiki/Academic_quarter_(year_division)" title="Academic quarter (year division)">quarter system</a>. There are three terms in the normal academic year: fall, winter, and spring, as well as a summer term. At the beginning of each term, there are one to three days of Pre-instructional Activities, where faculty meet to discuss instructional plans. During this period, students acquaint themselves to the campus and have the opportunity to take placement tests. At the end of each term, one week is devoted to final exams and special academic activities. There are 146 days of instruction, with a minimum of 48 per term.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_activities_and_traditions">Student activities and traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Student activities and traditions">edit</a>]</span></h2>
