     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social">Social</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Social">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>UCSB is a politically active campus. For the 2008 presidential election, UCSB won a national college competition for student voter registration by registering 10857 voters, or 51.5% of the student population.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The UCSB Campus Democrats are one of the most active organizations on campus. Over the years, other political parties and organizations have also been known to be active on campus, such as the Environmental Affairs Board, <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_(United_States)" title="Green Party (United States)" class="mw-redirect">Green Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Party_(United_States)" title="Libertarian Party (United States)">Libertarians</a>, <a href="/wiki/NORML" title="NORML" class="mw-redirect">NORML</a>, and the Queer Student Union.<sup id="cite_ref-UCSN_Queer_Student_Union_Webpage_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCSN_Queer_Student_Union_Webpage-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>There are a variety of on campus centers offering social, recreational, religious, and preprofessional activities for students. The UCSB Multicultural Center puts on numerous activities every year to support students of color and promote awareness of diversity issues on campus. Other organizations and centers include the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Nexus" title="Daily Nexus">Daily Nexus</a></i>, a daily newspaper, the La Cumbre Yearbook, the school radio station, <a href="/wiki/KCSB_91.9FM_Santa_Barbara" title="KCSB 91.9FM Santa Barbara" class="mw-redirect">KCSB 91.9</a>, <i>The Bottom Line</i>, a weekly newspaper, and the Gaucho Free Press, the campus's conservative magazine. The UCSB Recreation Center also hosts a variety of activities, from Adventure Programs to <a href="/wiki/Ballroom_dancing" title="Ballroom dancing" class="mw-redirect">ballroom dancing</a> classes. Further UCSB <a href="/wiki/Hillel:_The_Foundation_for_Jewish_Campus_Life" title="Hillel: The Foundation for Jewish Campus Life">Hillel</a> offers a space for UCSB's large Jewish population and a place for Jewish students to come together in a unique building in Isla Vista. Students socialize at the <a href="/wiki/UCSB_Arbor" title="UCSB Arbor" class="mw-redirect">Arbor</a>, the <a href="/wiki/UCSB_UCen" title="UCSB UCen" class="mw-redirect">UCen</a>, the Coral Tree Cafe the Courtyard Cafe and for a special lunch, the Faculty Club.</p> 
     <p>UCSB is also known for its annual free music festival, <a href="/wiki/Extravaganza_(Music_Festival)" title="Extravaganza (Music Festival)" class="mw-redirect">Extravaganza</a>. It is held at Harder Stadium in the spring and generally attracts around 8,000 people. Past performers have included <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/T.I." title="T.I.">T.I.</a>, <a href="/wiki/E-40" title="E-40">E-40</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sublime_(band)" title="Sublime (band)">Sublime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Run-D.M.C." title="Run-D.M.C." class="mw-redirect">Run-D.M.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Pharcyde" title="The Pharcyde">The Pharcyde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_Distortion" title="Social Distortion">Social Distortion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Johnson_(musician)" title="Jack Johnson (musician)">Jack Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)" class="mw-redirect">Drake</a> and <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a> amongst many others.</p> 
     <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
     <p>The Nu chapter of <a href="/wiki/Phrateres" title="Phrateres">Phrateres</a>, a non-exclusive, non-profit social-service club, was installed here in 1939. Between 1924 and 1967, 23 chapters of Phrateres were installed in universities across North America.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:San_Nicolas,_UCSB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/San_Nicolas%2C_UCSB.jpg/220px-San_Nicolas%2C_UCSB.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/San_Nicolas%2C_UCSB.jpg/330px-San_Nicolas%2C_UCSB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/San_Nicolas%2C_UCSB.jpg/440px-San_Nicolas%2C_UCSB.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:San_Nicolas,_UCSB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> San Nicolas residence hall. As of September 2008, six of the on-campus residence halls are named after the islands in the nearby 
        <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands_of_California" title="Channel Islands of California">Channel Islands</a> chain.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:De_La_Guerra_dining_common,_UCSB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/De_La_Guerra_dining_common%2C_UCSB.jpg/220px-De_La_Guerra_dining_common%2C_UCSB.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/De_La_Guerra_dining_common%2C_UCSB.jpg/330px-De_La_Guerra_dining_common%2C_UCSB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/De_La_Guerra_dining_common%2C_UCSB.jpg/440px-De_La_Guerra_dining_common%2C_UCSB.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:De_La_Guerra_dining_common,_UCSB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> De La Guerra dining commons
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>There are eight <a href="/wiki/Residence_halls" title="Residence halls" class="mw-redirect">residence halls</a> at UCSB, seven of which are located at the main campus. One, Santa Catalina, is located near the entrance to West Campus north of Isla Vista.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Santa Catalina has its own dining commons, Portola Dining Commons, as well as a heated swimming pool, two lounges, numerous study rooms, two recreational rooms, a gym, as well as tennis courts and an expansive lawn. Because Santa Catalina is nearly 1&nbsp;mi (1.6&nbsp;km) off-campus, it has its own campus police station as well as housing offices and Res-Net support center.</p> 
     <p>The Main Campus residence halls are found in two different locations. On the east end of campus are the residence halls named after five of the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands_of_California" title="Channel Islands of California">Channel Islands</a>: <a href="/wiki/Santa_Rosa_Island,_California" title="Santa Rosa Island, California">Santa Rosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz_Island" title="Santa Cruz Island">Santa Cruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anacapa_Island" title="Anacapa Island">Anacapa</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel_Island" title="San Miguel Island">San Miguel</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Nicolas_Island" title="San Nicolas Island">San Nicolas</a>. There are two dining commons located near the Channel Islands residence halls. The Ortega Dining Commons is located between San Miguel and the University Center <a href="/wiki/UCSB_UCen" title="UCSB UCen" class="mw-redirect">(UCen)</a>, and the De La Guerra Dining Commons (DLG) is located between Santa Rosa, Santa Cruz, and San Nicolas.</p> 
     <p>The two other residence halls, San Rafael and <a href="/wiki/Manzanita_Village" title="Manzanita Village" class="mw-redirect">Manzanita Village</a>, are located on the west side of campus and primarily house continuing and transfer students. The Carrillo Dining Commons is located in <a href="/wiki/Manzanita_Village" title="Manzanita Village" class="mw-redirect">Manzanita Village</a>, right next to San Rafael Hall. Manzanita Village was completed in 2002, and is the newest residence hall on campus.</p> 
     <p>In addition, the university also has four housing complexes for graduate students and their families: the recently completed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2012)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=San_Clemente_Villages&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="San Clemente Villages (page does not exist)">San Clemente Villages</a> for single graduate students, Santa Ynez Apartments, El Dorado Apartments, Westgate Apartments, and family student housing: West Campus Apartments and the Storke Apartment complexes. There is also Faculty Housing at the West Campus Point and new construction underway at the North Campus.</p> 
     <p>Private residence halls are also available to UCSB students. Tropicana Del Norte, located directly adjacent to the Main Campus, houses UCSB students in 51 furnished suites and has an on-site dining hall and heated pool.</p> 
     <p>Students may also choose to rent housing in the bordering community of Isla Vista. An estimated average for rent costs is $500?$800 US/month to share a bedroom, and includes trash pickup and water utilities. Low-cost housing is limited, with the cheapest source being the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara_Student_Housing_Cooperative" title="Santa Barbara Student Housing Cooperative">Santa Barbara Student Housing Cooperative</a>.</p> 
     <p>Other sources of housing include the Greek System, and outlying communities (i.e. Goleta, Santa Barbara, Isla Vista, Montecito). Some students live in Isla Vista, which is immediately adjacent to campus. Isla Vista since the early 1960s has a reputation of being a party environment. UCSB is also affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara_Student_Housing_Cooperative" title="Santa Barbara Student Housing Cooperative">Santa Barbara Student Housing Cooperative</a> in Isla Vista, which seeks to provide low rent co-op housing regardless of gender, race, social, political, or religious affiliation, and thereby influencing the community to eliminate prejudice and discrimination in the community.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>There are a number of academic resources offered by the university, including a <a href="/wiki/Writing_center" title="Writing center">writing center</a>, open <a href="/wiki/Computer_lab" title="Computer lab">computer labs</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Machining" title="Machining">machine shop</a>, and drop-in academic advising.</p> 
     <p>A large Recreation Center provides classes and facilities for students and faculty. The Center has swimming pools, <a href="/wiki/Racquetball" title="Racquetball">racquetball</a> courts, a rock wall, and exercise machines. The University Center has facilities for meetings and presentations, and also contains a bookstore, restaurants and a cashier.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UCSB has a health clinic. Students with ailments or seeking medical assistance may consult a physician at the clinic. The clinic also offers basic health care and provides emergency medicine and contraceptives. The university is the only UC campus with its own Paramedic Rescue Unit. It is staffed by full-time professional paramedics and part-time undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Emergency_medical_technician" title="Emergency medical technician">EMTs</a>.</p> 
     <p>SexInfo, which was started in 1976 by Professors John and Janice Baldwin, is run by students doing advanced course work and research on <a href="/wiki/Sexology" title="Sexology">sexuality</a> through UCSB's <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">Sociology</a> Department. The site is dedicated to providing accurate information about sexuality in a way that is both informative and personal. SexInfo answers questions sent in by readers from all over the world, as well as regularly updates and posts articles on various topics related to human sexuality. This program helps students getting their degree in psychology.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_Student_Programs">Free Student Programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Free Student Programs">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Campus Learning Assistance Services (CLAS): This program provides course-specific tutoring as well as academic skills development. Over 7,000 students use these free services each year, proving it to be an essential component to academic success at UCSB.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/University_of_California_Education_Abroad_Program" title="University of California Education Abroad Program">Education Abroad Program</a> (EAP) Though all Universities of California share this study abroad program, each one must individually seek out funds in order to ensure longevity. The main goal is to &quot;equip UC students with the knowledge, understanding, and skills for work and life in a globally interdependent and culturally diverse world.&quot; Students can choose from over 250 programs within 36 countries around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Education Opportunity Program (EOP): This program helps provide support and information base aiming to keep students actively participating in the campus academic community. A main goal is to keep student encouraged by giving a sense of belonging. &quot;EOP helps motivate and inform students to utilize services to enhance their preparation for the job market and/or graduate/professional school admission,&quot; among other things. Although any student can take advantage of what EOP offers, serving low-income and first-generation undergraduates is the main focus.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>MultiCultural Center (MCC): The mission of the MCC is to represent students of color, and provide awareness and education to the student body as a whole about <a href="/wiki/Cultural_diversity" title="Cultural diversity">cultural diversity</a>. &quot;In addition to continuing to provide a safe space for students of color, international students, and gay, lesbian, and bisexual students, the MCC serves as a bridge to the entire campus community. To that end, the MCC offers a broad spectrum of events including lectures, panel discussions, films and videos, musical, dance, and dramatic performances, and poetry readings, which are all open to the general public.&quot; The MCC has many facilities, including a lounge/gallery, theater, meeting room, and kitchen.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Career and Counseling Services: UCSB students as well as graduates are linked to the outside job market through this on-campus facility. Doors are open on weekdays allowing for students to drop in for advice, however appointments are recommended. While the online service Gaucholink is always available, the career fairs held are the primary way students successfully seek out a job or internship.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Campus Security Organization (CSO): This organization was created over 30 years ago acting as a liaison or mediator between students and residents of neighboring <a href="/wiki/Isla_Vista,_California" title="Isla Vista, California">Isla Vista</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Campus_police" title="Campus police">local police department</a>. A few of the CSO goals are to provide a safe and aware environment for students, to establish an open line of communication on a peer group level, and to maintain a positive relationship between the students and police.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Senior Class Gift: Each year, the graduating class chooses a program of students? choice to support as they leave UCSB. It is meant to act as a long-lasting legacy that students leave. Some notable gifts in the past went towards the Recreational Sports Legacy Fund and the Associated Students <a href="/wiki/Food_Bank" title="Food Bank" class="mw-redirect">Food Bank</a>. Many classes also decide to support the Alumni Association Scholarship Fund in addition.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding">Funding</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Funding">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The UCSB Annual Fund is the <a href="/wiki/Nonprofit_organization" title="Nonprofit organization">nonprofit organization</a> on campus that helps raise money to keep free programs available for students. About 250 gauchos per year call 40,000 parents and alumni in order to raise awareness of the financial situation the university is in. These students act as the mediator between the free programs and the donors by giving information about programs in need and helping keep them alive. The Office of Development is grateful for the support it receives in order to continue ?creating new, innovative fields of study, and preparing students for leadership in the new millennium.? Currently, Brandon Friesen is the director and Deven Desai is the assistant director.</p> 
     <p>The Hollister Research Center was the original location. In 2010, the fundraising moved on campus to Phelps Hall, where it can be found to this day. Students use an automated calling system in order to reach the large amount of parents and alumni associated to the university.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/UC_Santa_Barbara_Gauchos" title="UC Santa Barbara Gauchos">UC Santa Barbara Gauchos</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The mascot of UCSB is the <a href="/wiki/Gaucho" title="Gaucho">Gaucho</a> and the school colors are blue and gold. UCSB's sports teams compete in the <a href="/wiki/Big_West_Conference" title="Big West Conference">Big West Conference</a>, with the exception of the men's water polo, men's and women's swimming, and the men's volleyball teams, which are in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a>. Santa Barbara is best known for its women's basketball and <a href="/wiki/UCSB_soccer" title="UCSB soccer" class="mw-redirect">men's soccer</a> teams. In 2006, UCSB won their first NCAA Men's Soccer title and its second overall NCAA championship (1979 water polo) in school history.<sup id="cite_ref-ncaas_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ncaas-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:NewUCSBLogo.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/33/NewUCSBLogo.png/250px-NewUCSBLogo.png" width="250" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/33/NewUCSBLogo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/33/NewUCSBLogo.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:NewUCSBLogo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> UCSB's athletics logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>While there are some 400 students in ICA, there are over 700 in Club Sports Teams including: <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing" title="Alpine skiing">Alpine Racing</a>, Cycling, <a href="/wiki/Fencing" title="Fencing">Fencing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Field_Hockey" title="Field Hockey" class="mw-redirect">Field Hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/UC_Santa_Barbara_Gauchos_men%27s_lacrosse" title="UC Santa Barbara Gauchos men's lacrosse" class="mw-redirect">Lacrosse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roller_Hockey" title="Roller Hockey" class="mw-redirect">Roller Hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">Rugby</a>, Sailing, Soccer, <a href="/wiki/Triathlon" title="Triathlon">Triathlon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Frisbee" title="Ultimate Frisbee" class="mw-redirect">Ultimate Frisbee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_Ski" title="Water Ski" class="mw-redirect">Water Ski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">Rowing</a>. Many of these teams are highly regarded and compete against Intercollegiate teams from across the US. For example <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">Rowing</a> has produced several national team members including Nine-time National Rowing Team member Amy Fuller, winner of several Olympic and World Championship medals and currently head of the <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a> Rowing Program. The UCSB Cycling Team has also produced several national team members, Olympians, and members of numerous US and international professional teams.</p> 
     <p>Many other hundreds of students participate in a large Intramural program consisting of Badminton, Basketball, Bowling, Flag Football, Golf, Floor Hockey, Indoor and Outdoor Soccer, Racquetball, Squash, Running, Softball, Tennis, Table Tennis, Ultimate Frisbee, Volleyball, Inner tube water polo, and Kickball.</p> 
     <p>One non-sanctioned sport also draws many students to UCSB: surfing. The on-campus beaches include a number of decent surfing sites, including &quot;Poles,&quot; &quot;Campus Point,&quot; &quot;Depressions&quot; and &quot;Sands&quot; and &quot;Devereaux Point&quot; on the west campus. Because Campus Beach actually faces South and East, and is shielded by the Santa Barbara Channel Islands, the surf is usually quite small. However, a large North or West swell can wrap in to create great waves which are typically very clean and good for surfing. UCSB has a surf team that competes in NSSA (National Scholastic Surfing Association) competitions, and is generally considered one of the best in the nation. They continued their reputation by winning a record 14th National Title at the college level in 2010's finals.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>UCSB has refused to hire the disabled for certain jobs such as exam proctors and note takers.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> UCSB student Alexander Stern filed a lawsuit in federal court, <i>Alexander Stern v. Regents of the University of California</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> as a response to the ban on disability hiring.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 2012, the case has been settled.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: People">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara_people" title="List of University of California, Santa Barbara people">List of University of California, Santa Barbara people</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty">Notable faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_California,_Santa_Barbara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Notable faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Current UCSB faculty have received several prestigious awards, including five <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prizes" title="Nobel Prizes" class="mw-redirect">Nobel Prizes</a><sup id="cite_ref-nobel1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobel1-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nobel2_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobel2-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nobel3_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobel3-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nobel4_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobel4-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nobel5_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobel5-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, there are 25 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-memb_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-memb-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> 24 members of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-naoe_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-naoe-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> and 21 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">Academy of Arts and Sciences</a> on the faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-aaas_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaas-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Allison_Anders" title="Allison Anders">Allison Anders</a>, American film and television director</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Capps" title="Walter Capps">Walter Holden Capps</a> (1934?1997)&nbsp;? also known as Walter H. Capps&nbsp;? Democrat. Religious Studies professor. U.S. Representative from California 22nd District, 1997; (defeated, 1994) died in office 1997</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Nick_Carter_(athlete)" title="Nick Carter (athlete)">Nick Carter</a> 1928 Olympian, track coach 1939?1958</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Glen_Culler" title="Glen Culler">Glen Culler</a>, Professor of <a href="/wiki/Electrical_Engineering" title="Electrical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Electrical Engineering</a>, principal investigator for UCSB ARPAnet</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Freedman" title="Michael Freedman">Michael Freedman</a>, 1986 <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medalist</a> and director of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://stationq.ucsb.edu/">Microsoft Station Q</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Kip_Fulbeck" title="Kip Fulbeck">Kip Fulbeck</a>, Professor of Art, author, and artist exploring <a href="/wiki/Hapa" title="Hapa">Hapa</a> identity</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Gazzaniga" title="Michael Gazzaniga">Michael Gazzaniga</a>, Director of the SAGE Center for the Study of the Mind and Professor of <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">Psychology</a>, leading researcher in the field of <a href="/wiki/Cognitive_neuroscience" title="Cognitive neuroscience">cognitive neuroscience</a></li> 
      <li>Colin Gardner, Professor of Integrative Studies/Critical Theory, Departments of Art, Film &amp; Media Studies, Comparative Literature, and the History of Art and Architecture</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Howard_Giles" title="Howard Giles">Howard Giles</a>, Professor of <a href="/wiki/Communication" title="Communication">Communication</a>, creator of <a href="/wiki/Communication_accommodation_theory" title="Communication accommodation theory">communication accommodation theory</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Frank_Goodchild" title="Michael Frank Goodchild">Michael Frank Goodchild</a>, Professor of <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">Geography</a>, winner of the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Laur%C3%A9at_Prix_International_de_G%C3%A9ographie_Vautrin_Lud" title="Laur&eacute;at Prix International de G&eacute;ographie Vautrin Lud">Laur&eacute;at Prix International de G&eacute;ographie Vautrin Lud</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/David_J._Gross" title="David J. Gross" class="mw-redirect">David J. Gross</a>, Director of the <a href="/wiki/Kavli_Institute_for_Theoretical_Physics" title="Kavli Institute for Theoretical Physics">Kavli Institute for Theoretical Physics</a> and 2004 Nobel Laureate in <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a><sup id="cite_ref-bio3_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio3-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Alan_J._Heeger" title="Alan J. Heeger">Alan J. Heeger</a>, Professor of <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Materials" title="Materials" class="mw-redirect">Materials</a> and 2000 Nobel Laureate in <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">Chemistry</a><sup id="cite_ref-bio4_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio4-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Immanuel_C.Y._Hsu" title="Immanuel C.Y. Hsu">Immanuel C.Y. Hsu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sinologist" title="Sinologist" class="mw-redirect">sinologist</a> and Emeritus Professor of History</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Jacob_Israelachvili" title="Jacob Israelachvili">Jacob Israelachvili</a>, Professor of <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Engineering" title="Chemical Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Chemical Engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Materials" title="Materials" class="mw-redirect">Materials</a>, Elected Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_London" title="Royal Society of London" class="mw-redirect">Royal Society of London</a>, 1988<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Charles_Kolstad" title="Charles Kolstad">Charles Kolstad</a>, Chair of the Economics Department and Professor of Environmental Economics</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Kohn" title="Walter Kohn">Walter Kohn</a>, Founding director, Kavli Institute for Theoretical Physics, Research Professor of Physics and 1998 Nobel Laureate in Chemistry<sup id="cite_ref-bio6_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio6-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Herbert_Kroemer" title="Herbert Kroemer">Herbert Kroemer</a>, Professor of <a href="/wiki/Electrical_and_Computer_Engineering" title="Electrical and Computer Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Electrical and Computer Engineering</a> and of Materials and 2000 Nobel Laureate in Physics<sup id="cite_ref-bio5_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio5-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Finn_E._Kydland" title="Finn E. Kydland">Finn E. Kydland</a>, Professor of Economics and 2004 Nobel Laureate in Economics<sup id="cite_ref-bio2_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio2-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/L._Gary_Leal" title="L. Gary Leal">L. Gary Leal</a>, Warren &amp; Katharine Schlinger Professor of Chemical Engineering<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Luis_Leal_(writer)" title="Luis Leal (writer)">Luis Leal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexican-American" title="Mexican-American" class="mw-redirect">Mexican-American</a> writer and literary critic</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Bruce_H._Lipshutz" title="Bruce H. Lipshutz">Bruce H. Lipshutz</a>, Professor of <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">Chemistry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">Biochemistry</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Harold_Lewis" title="Harold Lewis">Harold Lewis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">Emeritus</a> Professor of <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a> and former department chairman</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/William_W._Murdoch" title="William W. Murdoch">William W. Murdoch</a>, Charles A. Storke II professor of <a href="/wiki/Population_ecology" title="Population ecology">population ecology</a>, recipient of the 1990 Robert H. <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Award" title="MacArthur Award" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur Award</a>, and <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">AAAS</a> Fellow known for his research in population regulation, biological control, and predator-prey relationships<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Shuji_Nakamura" title="Shuji Nakamura">Shuji Nakamura</a>, Japanese inventor of the bright green, white and blue <a href="/wiki/Gallium_nitride" title="Gallium nitride">GaN</a> <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">LEDs</a> and a blue laser. Recipient of the Millennium Technology Prize from the Finnish government in 2006<sup id="cite_ref-bio7_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio7-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/John_Nathan" title="John Nathan">John Nathan</a>, Takashima Professor of Japanese Cultural Studies and Emmy-award winning director of several documentaries<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Galen_D._Stucky" title="Galen D. Stucky">Galen D. Stucky</a>, E. Khashoggi Industries, LLC Professor in Letters and Science, Professor of <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">Chemistry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biochemistry" title="Biochemistry">Biochemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Materials" title="Materials" class="mw-redirect">Materials</a> Departments<sup id="cite_ref-bio8_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bio8-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/James_Thomson_(cell_biologist)" title="James Thomson (cell biologist)">James A. Thomson</a>, Adjunct Professor ? Molecular, Cellular &amp; Developmental Biology, &quot;father of stem-cell research&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Vanderpool" title="Jennifer Vanderpool">Jennifer Vanderpool</a> American Artist, Art Department<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul>

      <li><a href="/wiki/Skip_Schumaker" title="Skip Schumaker">Skip Schumaker</a> ? Major league 2nd baseman (<a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Brian_Shaw" title="Brian Shaw">Brian Shaw</a> ? Former NBA basketball player (Celtics, Magic, Heat, Lakers) and currently associate head coach for the Indiana Pacers.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Sipchen" title="Bob Sipchen">Bob Sipchen</a> 1976, Pulitzer Prize winning journalist, author (Baby Insane and the Buddha) and Communications Director, Sierra Club</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/L._J._Smith_(author)" title="L. J. Smith (author)">L. J. Smith</a> ? 1987, young-adult literature writer</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Bahar_Soomekh" title="Bahar Soomekh">Bahar Soomekh</a> ? 1997, actress</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Andrew_Smith" title="Mark Andrew Smith">Mark Andrew Smith</a> ? Graphic Novelist</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Chris_Speier" title="Chris Speier">Chris Speier</a> ? All-Star shortstop for <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> (did not graduate)</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Ryan_Spilborghs" title="Ryan Spilborghs">Ryan Spilborghs</a> ? Major League Outfielder</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Charissa_Thompson" title="Charissa Thompson">Charissa Thompson</a> ? Host of <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>'s Numbers Never Lie</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Brian_Townsend" title="Brian Townsend">Brian Townsend</a> ? Professional Poker Player and co-owner of <a href="/wiki/CardRunners" title="CardRunners">CardRunners</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Knut_Volleb%C3%A6k" title="Knut Volleb&aelig;k">Knut Volleb&aelig;k</a> ? Former <a href="/wiki/Foreign_minister_of_Norway" title="Foreign minister of Norway" class="mw-redirect">Foreign minister of Norway</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Craig_Wilson_(water_polo)" title="Craig Wilson (water polo)">Craig Wilson</a> - US National and Olympic Water Polo team goalie 1984-1992</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_C._Wilson" title="Joseph C. Wilson">Joseph C. Wilson</a> ? Former U.S. diplomat</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Young_(baseball)" title="Michael Young (baseball)">Michael Young</a> ? Perennial all star major league shortstop/third baseman for Texas Rangers</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Harris_Faulkner" title="Harris Faulkner">Harris Faulkner</a> ? is an American newscaster and television host for Fox News Channel</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Ra%27ad_Siraj" title="Ra'ad Siraj">Ra'ad Siraj</a> - Managing Director of <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_New_York_Mellon" title="Bank of New York Mellon" class="mw-redirect">Bank of New York Mellon</a></li> 
     </ul>
